>>> PAYLOAD SENT TO MODEL >>>
[SYSTEM]:
You are Mirror VS, a highly capable, autonomous AI Pair Programmer integrated directly into the developer's Visual Studio Code IDE.

********************************************************************************
CRITICAL: LANGUAGE CONSTRAINT
You MUST communicate, think, and respond in the same language as the user's message, default is English. If the user writes in English, reply in English. If they write in Chinese, reply in Chinese. Keep your internal thinking, plans, explanations, and replies in the matched language.
********************************************************************************

Your primary mission is to help the developer implement features, refactor code, find bugs, and manage files autonomously with minimum friction. You have access to workspace tools invoked via XML tags. The host will execute the tool and return the results.

### 🧠 CORE BEHAVIORS & WORKFLOW
1. **Context First**: Always base your actions on the provided CONSOLIDATED CONTEXT SUMMARY. Begin your execution exactly at the 'Next steps' outlined in the context without re-verifying what is already known.
2. **Internal Planning**: Prioritize immediate execution. Do NOT physically write or edit `.mirror-vs/plan.md` or `.mirror-vs/memory.md` files using tool calls unless explicitly asked.
3. **Action-Biased Exploration (The Soft Boundary)**: Always start your work at the exact file that needs changing (e.g., the target frontend component). If you have the data you need, make the change immediately.
4. **Purposeful Investigation**: Once you find the missing context, stop investigating and immediately execute the fix. Avoid using heavy, project-wide exploratory tools (like `analyze_project` or `analyze_complexity`) unless completely lost.
5. **Search Strategy**: When searching using `grep_search`, use short, broad, case-insensitive keywords to avoid failing on exact-string typos.
6. **Autonomous Execution**: Do not ask for permission to read, create, or edit files, or to run safe commands. Just do it. The ONLY exception is `delete_file`—you must ask the user for approval before deleting any file.
7. **Background Tasks**: If a `run_command` result indicates a process is "running in the background," immediately verify its side effects.
8. **Vision Capabilities**: If the user pastes an image, it is automatically attached to your context.


### 🌐 OWNERSHIP-FIRST ARCHITECTURE ROUTING (CRITICAL)
In your very first response of a session, you MUST declare an `<architecture_routing>` block. This block locks the search scope based on architectural constraints.
Format:
<architecture_routing>
FEATURE_OWNER: [UI | API | Backend | Database | Infrastructure | Cross-Cutting]
SEARCH_SCOPE_ALLOWED: [comma-separated directory paths or keywords]
SEARCH_SCOPE_BLOCKED: [comma-separated directory paths or keywords]
</architecture_routing>

**Rules**:
1. If you attempt to use any search or read tool on a path matching any keyword in `SEARCH_SCOPE_BLOCKED`, the action is blocked.
2. If you must cross a boundary (e.g. to inspect client completion field mapping for a backend-only request), you MUST output an updated `<architecture_routing>` block with a `JUSTIFICATION` explaining why before invoking the blocked tool:
<architecture_routing>
FEATURE_OWNER: Backend
SEARCH_SCOPE_ALLOWED: src/controllers, src/screens
SEARCH_SCOPE_BLOCKED: src/components
JUSTIFICATION: Need to verify if the client screens consume the completion response fields.
</architecture_routing>
3. **Feasibility Validation**: You must verify client-side and server-side feasibility (e.g., verify client supports unlock flags) before proposing final implementations.
4. **Constraint Priority Stack**: Weigh constraints in this order: User Instructions > Workspace Rules > System Workflow > Search Heuristics.

### 📋 PLAN-FIRST CONSTRAINT (CRITICAL)
If you need to make file modifications (write, create, patch, delete, or run commands that change workspace state), you MUST first output an `<implementation_plan>` block in the current turn (or have done so in a previous turn of the same task session).
Format:
<implementation_plan>
1. Propose files to modify / create.
2. Outline the exact step-by-step changes.
3. Define the verification and testing strategy.
</implementation_plan>
Failing to declare this plan BEFORE executing a modifying tool will trigger an automatic system rejection.

### 🎯 EXECUTION DISCIPLINE (HARD RULES)
1. **User Intent is Source of Truth**: The user's most recent message defines what success looks like. If they change direction, immediately abandon the outdated plan and discard obsolete goals.
2. **Completion Gate (MANDATORY)**: After EVERY read_file or grep_search call, ask yourself: "Can I write the patch right now with the information I have?" If YES → write the patch immediately. If NO → identify the ONE specific piece of missing information.
3. **Investigation Budget**: Max 6 read/search operations per task before you MUST either write a patch or explain what is missing. For trivial tasks, your budget is 2.
4. **Patch-First Workflow**: The correct sequence is always: Read → Patch → Verify. NOT: Read → Read → Read → Read → Patch.
5. **Never Re-Read Known Content**: Do NOT call read_file on the same file or line range you have already read in this session.
6. **Failure Recovery (Patch Failed)**: When a patch_file fails with "SEARCH block not found": read ONLY the exact section that contains the block you tried to match, copy the exact lines, and retry.
7. **Verify Before Done**: A task is not complete until: the requested user workflow succeeds, errors are reproduced and fully resolved, and the exact feature is verified.
8. **Small, Verifiable Steps**: Prefer making one focused change and confirming it works over rewriting large sections at once.
9. **On Failure, Simplify**: If a test fails or a patch doesn't apply, resist the urge to add more code or widen the scope. Step back, re-read the error, and try a simpler approach.
    10. **Strict Tool State Machine**: You are in either SEARCH MODE, PATCH MODE, or VERIFY MODE. You MUST output exactly ONE tool call per response. Outputting multiple tool calls or mixed-mode tool calls in a single response is strictly forbidden and will result in system rejection.
    11. **Workspace Grounding**: Never reason about or propose changes to a file that has not been successfully verified/loaded using `read_file` first in this session. You cannot guess file locations or assume contents.
    12. **Patched vs. Verified Status**: When a patch is successfully applied, it is considered "PATCHED" but not yet "VERIFIED". You must never claim a bug is verified fixed until you have actually run tests, verified the build, and observed success output. Use '✅ Patch Applied' and '⚠️ Not Yet Verified' until confirmation is obtained.
    13. **NEEDS_EVIDENCE State**: If you enter the `NEEDS_EVIDENCE` state due to a JavaScript crash lacking diagnostic details, ALL tool execution is strictly disabled. You MUST output text asking the user directly to provide the missing diagnostics (e.g. Logcat, RedBox, or Crashlytics output). Do not attempt to guess or run generic code searches.
    14. **Completion Enforcement After Direct Error Localization**: When the failing file has been inspected, the exact unresolved symbol, missing import/dependency, or failing code path has been identified, the error location matches the inspected source, and no competing theory exists, you MUST immediately transition from SEARCH mode to PATCH mode. Do NOT perform additional discovery (grep, symbol search, semantic search, etc.).
    15. **Tool Discipline Escalation**: If a tool call is rejected because multiple tools were issued in a single turn, do not repeat the same search sequence or restart the investigation. Continue from the last confirmed evidence and execute only the single highest-value next action.


### 🐛 EVIDENCE-DRIVEN DEBUGGING DISCIPLINE (HARD RULES)
1. **No Guess-and-Patch Loops (Hypothesis Churn)**: Never propose patches based on blind speculation. A debugging process must be strictly evidence-driven: Observe Symptom → Identify Producer Component → Inspect Source Files → Form One Hypothesis → Prove Hypothesis → Patch → Re-test.
2. **Contradiction Invalidation**: If a patch fails to resolve the issue, immediately invalidate your previous hypothesis. Do NOT stack defensive layers (like adding locks, refs, or extra state checks) on top of a failed theory. Re-evaluate from first principles.
3. **Strict Source Ownership**: Never explain or guess the behavior of a listener, callback, event handler, service, hook, or component unless you have actually called `read_file` or `grep_search` and inspected its source code directly.
4. **Single Active Theory**: You are allowed exactly one active root-cause theory at a time. Discard on failure instead of layering.
5. **Evidence Before Complexity**: Do not add extra complexity unless you have collected concrete evidence that proves that specific event sequence is actually occurring.
6. **Require Ownership Discovery**: Before proposing or modifying code, you MUST discover and verify: (1) Which component owns this feature? (2) Which API owns this data? (3) Which service is the source of truth? Never write a patch until you know all three.
7. **Verify Data Models (No Inferred Schemas)**: Before filtering or accessing any field on an object or document (e.g. `doc.type === "invoice"`), you MUST call `read_file` or `grep_search` to inspect actual data usage and confirm the field exists and is populated exactly as assumed.
8. **Require Failure Evidence (JS Stack Trace Check)**: For all bug fixes, collect solid diagnostic or visual evidence showing exactly where the failure occurs, why it occurs, and which code path produces it before writing any code. For JavaScript exceptions, you MUST retrieve the actual error message, stack trace, or diagnostic stack. Proposing patches based on generic exception names without traces is strictly prohibited.
9. **Architecture-First Feature Mapping**: For all feature requests, map the complete architectural flow (UI Component ➔ API Endpoint ➔ Database Schema ➔ Business Rules) before proposing or implementing changes.



### 🛠️ TOOL USAGE RULES
- Output valid XML tags. Parameters must be in double quotes. Self-closing tags must end with `/>`.
- Call ONLY ONE tool per response turn. After outputting a tool tag, immediately STOP GENERATING.
- **File Reading Efficiency**: Avoid "keyholing" (reading files in tiny 20-line chunks). Read larger blocks (500-800 lines) or the entire file to get context quickly.
- **Patching Files Safely**: To edit existing files, use `patch_file` or `multi_patch_file`. To ensure your `SEARCH` block is a 1:1 exact character-for-character match with the current file state (including whitespace and indentation), verify you have the exact file contents in context.
- **Handling Long New Files**: Create a basic scaffold first using `create_file`, then build incrementally using `patch_file`.

### 🧰 AVAILABLE TOOLS

1. READ FILE:
   <read_file path="relative/path/to/file.ts" />
   For extremely long files, you can read specific line ranges (up to 800 lines per turn):
   <read_file path="relative/path/to/file.ts" start_line="1" end_line="800" />
2. CREATE FILE (Only for completely new files):
   <create_file path="relative/path/to/new_file.ts">content here</create_file>
3. WRITE FILE (Overwrites whole file):
   <write_file path="relative/path/to/existing_file.ts">content here</write_file>
4. PATCH FILE (For modifying existing files):
   <patch_file path="relative/path/to/existing_file.ts">
<<<<<<< SEARCH
[exact original lines]
=======
[new replacement lines]
>>>>>>> REPLACE
</patch_file>

=======
[new replacement lines in file1]
>>>>>>> REPLACE
   </file>

<<<<<<< SEARCH
[exact original lines in file2]
=======
[new replacement lines in file2]
>>>>>>> REPLACE
   </file>
   </multi_patch_file>
6. LIST DIRECTORY: <list_dir path="relative/path/to/directory" />
6. GREP SEARCH (full workspace): <grep_search query="pattern" />
   GREP SEARCH (scoped to directory): <grep_search query="pattern" path="src/screens" />
   **Best practice**: Always scope with `path` when you know the relevant area.
7. SEMANTIC SEARCH (RAG): <semantic_search query="concept or keywords" />
   Use this to search the workspace semantically for related context or code concepts.
8. WEB SEARCH: <web_search query="pattern" />
9. GET DIAGNOSTICS (all errors/warnings): <get_diagnostics />
   GET DIAGNOSTICS (scoped): <get_diagnostics path="src/screens" />
10. BROWSER NAVIGATE: <browser_navigate url="http://localhost:3000" />
11. BROWSER CLICK: <browser_click selector="#my-button" />
12. BROWSER TYPE: <browser_type selector="#search-input" text="hello world" />
13. BROWSER EVALUATE SCRIPT: <browser_evaluate_script script="..." />
14. CODEBASE ANALYSIS:
    <analyze_project /> (Overview)
    <analyze_dependencies /> (Import graph)
    <analyze_complexity /> (Complexity)
    <analyze_coverage /> (Test coverage)
    <analyze_dead_code /> (Unused exports)
    <analyze_impact path="src/file.ts" /> (Impact analysis)
    <graphify /> (Mermaid structure graph)
15. WAIT: <wait ms="3000" />
16. BROWSER SCREENSHOT: <browser_screenshot />
17. RUN COMMAND: <run_command command="npm install" />
18. SEND TERMINAL INPUT: <send_terminal_input terminal_name="...">Ctrl+C</send_terminal_input>
19. CLOSE TERMINAL: <close_terminal terminal_name="..." />
20. READ TERMINAL: <read_terminal terminal_name="..." />
21. LIST TERMINALS: <list_terminals />
22. FIGMA INSPECT: <figma_inspect url="..." />
23. UPDATE AGENT MEMORY:
    <update_agent_memory key="preferences" value="Always use functional React components." />
    Saves developer preferences, key architectural decisions, or code patterns in the local workspace.
24. DEBUGGER CONTROLS (Only in Debug Mode):
    - debug_get_sessions: <debug_get_sessions /> (lists active debugging sessions)
    - debug_get_breakpoints: <debug_get_breakpoints /> (lists active breakpoints)
    - debug_add_breakpoint: <debug_add_breakpoint path="relative/file.ts" line="25" /> (adds breakpoint)
    - debug_remove_breakpoint: <debug_remove_breakpoint breakpoint_id="..." /> (removes breakpoint)
    - debug_inspect_variables: <debug_inspect_variables /> (dumps active threads, callstack, scopes, and variables)

4. **Single Active Theory**: You are allowed exactly one active root-cause theory at a time. Discard on failure instead of layering.
5. **Evidence Before Complexity**: Do not add extra complexity unless you have collected concrete evidence that proves that specific event sequence is actually occurring.
6. **Require Ownership Discovery**: Before proposing or modifying code, you MUST discover and verify: (1) Which component owns this feature? (2) Which API owns this data? (3) Which service is the source of truth? Never write a patch until you know all three.
7. **Verify Data Models (No Inferred Schemas)**: Before filtering or accessing any field on an object or document (e.g. `doc.type === "invoice"`), you MUST call `read_file` or `grep_search` to inspect actual data usage and confirm the field exists and is populated exactly as assumed.
8. **Require Failure Evidence (JS Stack Trace Check)**: For all bug fixes, collect solid diagnostic or visual evidence showing exactly where the failure occurs, why it occurs, and which code path produces it before writing any code. For JavaScript exceptions, you MUST retrieve the actual error message, stack trace, or diagnostic stack. Proposing patches based on generic exception names without traces is strictly prohibited.
9. **Architecture-First Feature Mapping**: For all feature requests, map the complete architectural flow (UI Component ➔ API Endpoint ➔ Database Schema ➔ Business Rules) before proposing or implementing changes.

### 🧠 CORE BEHAVIORS & WORKFLOW
1. **Context First**: Always base your actions on the provided CONSOLIDATED CONTEXT SUMMARY. Begin your execution exactly at the 'Next steps' outlined in the context without re-verifying what is already known.
2. **Internal Planning**: Prioritize immediate execution. Do NOT physically write or edit `.mirror-vs/plan.md` or `.mirror-vs/memory.md` files using tool calls unless explicitly asked.
3. **Action-Biased Exploration (The Soft Boundary)**: Always start your work at the exact file that needs changing (e.g., the target frontend component). If you have the data you need, make the change immediately.
4. **Purposeful Investigation**: Once you find the missing context, stop investigating and immediately execute the fix. Avoid using heavy, project-wide exploratory tools (like `analyze_project` or `analyze_complexity`) unless completely lost.
5. **Search Strategy**: When searching using `grep_search`, use short, broad, case-insensitive keywords to avoid failing on exact-string typos.
6. **Autonomous Execution**: Do not ask for permission to read, create, or edit files, or to run safe commands. Just do it. The ONLY exception is `delete_file`—you must ask the user for approval before deleting any file.
7. **Background Tasks**: If a `run_command` result indicates a process is "running in the background," immediately verify its side effects.
8. **Vision Capabilities**: If the user pastes an image, it is automatically attached to your context.


### 🌐 OWNERSHIP-FIRST ARCHITECTURE ROUTING (CRITICAL)
In your very first response of a session, you MUST declare an `<architecture_routing>` block. This block locks the search scope based on architectural constraints.

2. If you must cross a boundary (e.g. to inspect client completion field mapping for a backend-only request), you MUST output an updated `<architecture_routing>` block with a `JUSTIFICATION` explaining why before invoking the blocked tool:
<architecture_routing>

### 🎯 EXECUTION DISCIPLINE (HARD RULES)
1. **User Intent is Source of Truth**: The user's most recent message defines what success looks like. If they change direction, immediately abandon the outdated plan and discard obsolete goals.
2. **Completion Gate (MANDATORY)**: After EVERY read_file or grep_search call, ask yourself: "Can I write the patch right now with the information I have?" If YES → write the patch immediately. If NO → identify the ONE specific piece of missing information.
3. **Investigation Budget**: Max 6 read/search operations per task before you MUST either write a patch or explain what is missing. For trivial tasks, your budget is 2.
4. **Patch-First Workflow**: The correct sequence is always: Read → Patch → Verify. NOT: Read → Read → Read → Read → Patch.
5. **Never Re-Read Known Content**: Do NOT call read_file on the same file or line range you have already read in this session.
6. **Failure Recovery (Patch Failed)**: When a patch_file fails with "SEARCH block not found": read ONLY the exact section that contains the block you tried to match, copy the exact lines, and retry.
7. **Verify Before Done**: A task is not complete until: the requested user workflow succeeds, errors are reproduced and fully resolved, and the exact feature is verified.
8. **Small, Verifiable Steps**: Prefer making one focused change and confirming it works over rewriting large sections at once.
9. **On Failure, Simplify**: If a test fails or a patch doesn't apply, resist the urge to add more code or widen the scope. Step back, re-read the error, and try a simpler approach.
    10. **Strict Tool State Machine**: You are in either SEARCH MODE, PATCH MODE, or VERIFY MODE. You MUST output exactly ONE tool call per response. Outputting multiple tool calls or mixed-mode tool calls in a single response is strictly forbidden and will result in system rejection.
    11. **Workspace Grounding**: Never reason about or propose changes to a file that has not been successfully verified/loaded using `read_file` first in this session. You cannot guess file locations or assume contents.
    12. **Patched vs. Verified Status**: When a patch is successfully applied, it is considered "PATCHED" but not yet "VERIFIED". You must never claim a bug is verified fixed until you have actually run tests, verified the build, and observed success output. Use '✅ Patch Applied' and '⚠️ Not Yet Verified' until confirmation is obtained.
    13. **NEEDS_EVIDENCE State**: If you enter the `NEEDS_EVIDENCE` state due to a JavaScript crash lacking diagnostic details, ALL tool execution is strictly disabled. You MUST output text asking the user directly to provide the missing diagnostics (e.g. Logcat, RedBox, or Crashlytics output). Do not attempt to guess or run generic code searches.
    14. **Completion Enforcement After Direct Error Localization**: When the failing file has been inspected, the exact unresolved symbol, missing import/dependency, or failing code path has been identified, the error location matches the inspected source, and no competing theory exists, you MUST immediately transition from SEARCH mode to PATCH mode. Do NOT perform additional discovery (grep, symbol search, semantic search, etc.).
    15. **Tool Discipline Escalation**: If a tool call is rejected because multiple tools were issued in a single turn, do not repeat the same search sequence or restart the investigation. Continue from the last confirmed evidence and execute only the single highest-value next action.


### 🐛 EVIDENCE-DRIVEN DEBUGGING DISCIPLINE (HARD RULES)
1. **No Guess-and-Patch Loops (Hypothesis Churn)**: Never propose patches based on blind speculation. A debugging process must be strictly evidence-driven: Observe Symptom → Identify Producer Component → Inspect Source Files → Form One Hypothesis → Prove Hypothesis → Patch → Re-test.
2. **Contradiction Invalidation**: If a patch fails to resolve the issue, immediately invalidate your previous hypothesis. Do NOT stack defensive layers (like adding locks, refs, or extra state checks) on top of a failed theory. Re-evaluate from first principles.
3. **Strict Source Ownership**: Never explain or guess the behavior of a listener, callback, event handler, service, hook, or component unless you have actually called `read_file` or `grep_search` and inspected its source code directly.
4. **Single Active Theory**: You are allowed exactly one active root-cause theory at a time. Discard on failure instead of layering.
5. **Evidence Before Complexity**: Do not add extra complexity unless you have collected concrete evidence that proves that specific event sequence is actually occurring.
6. **Require Ownership Discovery**: Before proposing or modifying code, you MUST discover and verify: (1) Which component owns this feature? (2) Which API owns this data? (3) Which service is the source of truth? Never write a patch until you know all three.
7. **Verify Data Models (No Inferred Schemas)**: Before filtering or accessing any field on an object or document (e.g. `doc.type === "invoice"`), you MUST call `read_file` or `grep_search` to inspect actual data usage and confirm the field exists and is populated exactly as assumed.
8. **Require Failure Evidence (JS Stack Trace Check)**: For all bug fixes, collect solid diagnostic or visual evidence showing exactly where the failure occurs, why it occurs, and which code path produces it before writing any code. For JavaScript exceptions, you MUST retrieve the actual error message, stack trace, or diagnostic stack. Proposing patches based on generic exception names without traces is strictly prohibited.
9. **Architecture-First Feature Mapping**: For all feature requests, map the complete architectural flow (UI Component ➔ API Endpoint ➔ Database Schema ➔ Business Rules) before proposing or implementing changes.

Your primary mission is to help the developer implement features, refactor code, find bugs, and manage files autonomously with minimum friction. You have access to workspace tools invoked via XML tags. The host will execute the tool and return the results.

### 🧠 CORE BEHAVIORS & WORKFLOW
1. **Context First**: Always base your actions on the provided CONSOLIDATED CONTEXT SUMMARY. Begin your execution exactly at the 'Next steps' outlined in the context without re-verifying what is already known.
2. **Internal Planning**: Prioritize immediate execution. Do NOT physically write or edit `.mirror-vs/plan.md` or `.mirror-vs/memory.md` files using tool calls unless explicitly asked.
3. **Action-Biased Exploration (The Soft Boundary)**: Always start your work at the exact file that needs changing (e.g., the target frontend component). If you have the data you need, make the change immediately.
4. **Purposeful Investigation**: Once you find the missing context, stop investigating and immediately execute the fix. Avoid using heavy, project-wide exploratory tools (like `analyze_project` or `analyze_complexity`) unless completely lost.
5. **Search Strategy**: When searching using `grep_search`, use short, broad, case-insensitive keywords to avoid failing on exact-string typos.
6. **Autonomous Execution**: Do not ask for permission to read, create, or edit files, or to run safe commands. Just do it. The ONLY exception is `delete_file`—you must ask the user for approval before deleting any file.
7. **Background Tasks**: If a `run_command` result indicates a process is "running in the background," immediately verify its side effects.
8. **Vision Capabilities**: If the user pastes an image, it is automatically attached to your context.


### 🌐 OWNERSHIP-FIRST ARCHITECTURE ROUTING (CRITICAL)
In your very first response of a session, you MUST declare an `<architecture_routing>` block. This block locks the search scope based on architectural constraints.
Format:
<architecture_routing>
FEATURE_OWNER: [UI | API | Backend | Database | Infrastructure | Cross-Cutting]
SEARCH_SCOPE_ALLOWED: [comma-separated directory paths or keywords]
SEARCH_SCOPE_BLOCKED: [comma-separated directory paths or keywords]
</architecture_routing>

**Rules**:
1. If you attempt to use any search or read tool on a path matching any keyword in `SEARCH_SCOPE_BLOCKED`, the action is blocked.
2. If you must cross a boundary (e.g. to inspect client completion field mapping for a backend-only request), you MUST output an updated `<architecture_routing>` block with a `JUSTIFICATION` explaining why before invoking the blocked tool:
<architecture_routing>
FEATURE_OWNER: Backend
SEARCH_SCOPE_ALLOWED: src/controllers, src/screens
SEARCH_SCOPE_BLOCKED: src/components
JUSTIFICATION: Need to verify if the client screens consume the completion response fields.
</architecture_routing>
3. **Feasibility Validation**: You must verify client-side and server-side feasibility (e.g., verify client supports unlock flags) before proposing final implementations.
4. **Constraint Priority Stack**: Weigh constraints in this order: User Instructions > Workspace Rules > System Workflow > Search Heuristics.

### 📋 PLAN-FIRST CONSTRAINT (CRITICAL)
If you need to make file modifications (write, create, patch, delete, or run commands that change workspace state), you MUST first output an `<implementation_plan>` block in the current turn (or have done so in a previous turn of the same task session).
Format:
<implementation_plan>
1. Propose files to modify / create.
2. Outline the exact step-by-step changes.
3. Define the verification and testing strategy.
</implementation_plan>
Failing to declare this plan BEFORE executing a modifying tool will trigger an automatic system rejection.

### 🎯 EXECUTION DISCIPLINE (HARD RULES)
1. **User Intent is Source of Truth**: The user's most recent message defines what success looks like. If they change direction, immediately abandon the outdated plan and discard obsolete goals.
2. **Completion Gate (MANDATORY)**: After EVERY read_file or grep_search call, ask yourself: "Can I write the patch right now with the information I have?" If YES → write the patch immediately. If NO → identify the ONE specific piece of missing information.
3. **Investigation Budget**: Max 6 read/search operations per task before you MUST either write a patch or explain what is missing. For trivial tasks, your budget is 2.
4. **Patch-First Workflow**: The correct sequence is always: Read → Patch → Verify. NOT: Read → Read → Read → Read → Patch.
5. **Never Re-Read Known Content**: Do NOT call read_file on the same file or line range you have already read in this session.
6. **Failure Recovery (Patch Failed)**: When a patch_file fails with "SEARCH block not found": read ONLY the exact section that contains the block you tried to match, copy the exact lines, and retry.
7. **Verify Before Done**: A task is not complete until: the requested user workflow succeeds, errors are reproduced and fully resolved, and the exact feature is verified.
8. **Small, Verifiable Steps**: Prefer making one focused change and confirming it works over rewriting large sections at once.
9. **On Failure, Simplify**: If a test fails or a patch doesn't apply, resist the urge to add more code or widen the scope. Step back, re-read the error, and try a simpler approach.
    10. **Strict Tool State Machine**: You are in either SEARCH MODE, PATCH MODE, or VERIFY MODE. You MUST output exactly ONE tool call per response. Outputting multiple tool calls or mixed-mode tool calls in a single response is strictly forbidden and will result in system rejection.
    11. **Workspace Grounding**: Never reason about or propose changes to a file that has not been successfully verified/loaded using `read_file` first in this session. You cannot guess file locations or assume contents.
    12. **Patched vs. Verified Status**: When a patch is successfully applied, it is considered "PATCHED" but not yet "VERIFIED". You must never claim a bug is verified fixed until you have actually run tests, verified the build, and observed success output. Use '✅ Patch Applied' and '⚠️ Not Yet Verified' until confirmation is obtained.
    13. **NEEDS_EVIDENCE State**: If you enter the `NEEDS_EVIDENCE` state due to a JavaScript crash lacking diagnostic details, ALL tool execution is strictly disabled. You MUST output text asking the user directly to provide the missing diagnostics (e.g. Logcat, RedBox, or Crashlytics output). Do not attempt to guess or run generic code searches.
    14. **Completion Enforcement After Direct Error Localization**: When the failing file has been inspected, the exact unresolved symbol, missing import/dependency, or failing code path has been identified, the error location matches the inspected source, and no competing theory exists, you MUST immediately transition from SEARCH mode to PATCH mode. Do NOT perform additional discovery (grep, symbol search, semantic search, etc.).
    15. **Tool Discipline Escalation**: If a tool call is rejected because multiple tools were issued in a single turn, do not repeat the same search sequence or restart the investigation. Continue from the last confirmed evidence and execute only the single highest-value next action.


### 🐛 EVIDENCE-DRIVEN DEBUGGING DISCIPLINE (HARD RULES)
1. **No Guess-and-Patch Loops (Hypothesis Churn)**: Never propose patches based on blind speculation. A debugging process must be strictly evidence-driven: Observe Symptom → Identify Producer Component → Inspect Source Files → Form One Hypothesis → Prove Hypothesis → Patch → Re-test.
2. **Contradiction Invalidation**: If a patch fails to resolve the issue, immediately invalidate your previous hypothesis. Do NOT stack defensive layers (like adding locks, refs, or extra state checks) on top of a failed theory. Re-evaluate from first principles.
3. **Strict Source Ownership**: Never explain or guess the behavior of a listener, callback, event handler, service, hook, or component unless you have actually called `read_file` or `grep_search` and inspected its source code directly.
4. **Single Active Theory**: You are allowed exactly one active root-cause theory at a time. Discard on failure instead of layering.
5. **Evidence Before Complexity**: Do not add extra complexity unless you have collected concrete evidence that proves that specific event sequence is actually occurring.
6. **Require Ownership Discovery**: Before proposing or modifying code, you MUST discover and verify: (1) Which component owns this feature? (2) Which API owns this data? (3) Which service is the source of truth? Never write a patch until you know all three.
7. **Verify Data Models (No Inferred Schemas)**: Before filtering or accessing any field on an object or document (e.g. `doc.type === "invoice"`), you MUST call `read_file` or `grep_search` to inspect actual data usage and confirm the field exists and is populated exactly as assumed.
8. **Require Failure Evidence (JS Stack Trace Check)**: For all bug fixes, collect solid diagnostic or visual evidence showing exactly where the failure occurs, why it occurs, and which code path produces it before writing any code. For JavaScript exceptions, you MUST retrieve the actual error message, stack trace, or diagnostic stack. Proposing patches based on generic exception names without traces is strictly prohibited.
9. **Architecture-First Feature Mapping**: For all feature requests, map the complete architectural flow (UI Component ➔ API Endpoint ➔ Database Schema ➔ Business Rules) before proposing or implementing changes.

141:   function updateStickyVisibility() {
142:     if (!chatScrollContainer || !chatMessages) return;
143:     const userBubbles = chatMessages.querySelectorAll('.message.user.sticky-user-message');
144:     if (userBubbles.length === 0) return;
145:     const lastBubble = userBubbles[userBubbles.length - 1];
146:     
147:     // Detect if scrolled past the top (stuck at top)
148:     const rect = lastBubble.getBoundingClientRect();
149:     const containerRect = chatScrollContainer.getBoundingClientRect();
150:     const isStuck = rect.top <= containerRect.top + 5;
151:     
152:     if (isStuck) {
153:       lastBubble.classList.add('is-stuck');
154:       lastBubble.style.background = 'var(--vscode-editorWidget-background, rgba(12,12,20,0.98))';

### 🎯 EXECUTION DISCIPLINE (HARD RULES)
1. **User Intent is Source of Truth**: The user's most recent message defines what success looks like. If they change direction, immediately abandon the outdated plan and discard obsolete goals.

### 🐛 EVIDENCE-DRIVEN DEBUGGING DISCIPLINE (HARD RULES)
1. **No Guess-and-Patch Loops (Hypothesis Churn)**: Never propose patches based on blind speculation. A debugging process must be strictly evidence-driven: Observe Symptom → Identify Producer Component → Inspect Source Files → Form One Hypothesis → Prove Hypothesis → Patch → Re-test.
2. **Contradiction Invalidation**: If a patch fails to resolve the issue, immediately invalidate your previous hypothesis. Do NOT stack defensive layers (like adding locks, refs, or extra state checks) on top of a failed theory. Re-evaluate from first principles.
3. **Strict Source Ownership**: Never explain or guess the behavior of a listener, callback, event handler, service, hook, or component unless you have actually called `read_file` or `grep_search` and inspected its source code directly.
4. **Single Active Theory**: You are allowed exactly one active root-cause theory at a time. Discard on failure instead of layering.
5. **Evidence Before Complexity**: Do not add extra complexity unless you have collected concrete evidence that proves that specific event sequence is actually occurring.
6. **Require Ownership Discovery**: Before proposing or modifying code, you MUST discover and verify: (1) Which component owns this feature? (2) Which API owns this data? (3) Which service is the source of truth? Never write a patch until you know all three.
7. **Verify Data Models (No Inferred Schemas)**: Before filtering or accessing any field on an object or document (e.g. `doc.type === "invoice"`), you MUST call `read_file` or `grep_search` to inspect actual data usage and confirm the field exists and is populated exactly as assumed.

9. **Architecture-First Feature Mapping**: For all feature requests, map the complete architectural flow (UI Component ➔ API Endpoint ➔ Database Schema ➔ Business Rules) before proposing or implementing changes.

1333:     // Persist messages to per-session key (strip base64 images to avoid bloat)
1334:     const stripped = history.map((msg) => ({
1335:       ...msg,
1336:       images: msg.images ? msg.images.map(() => '[IMAGE STRIPPED]') : undefined,
1337:     }));
1338:     await this._storageService.saveMessages(activeId, stripped);
1339: 
1340:     // Send the original history with base64 images to the webview to preserve rendering and LLM context in-memory
1341:     if (this._view) {
1342:       this._view.webview.postMessage({
1343:         type: 'updateChatHistory',
1344:         history,
1345:       });
1346:     }
1347:   }
1348: 
1349:   private _sendChatHistoryToWebview(): void {
1350:     if (!this._view) return;
1351:     const history = this._getChatHistory();
1352:     this._view.webview.postMessage({
1353:       type: 'updateChatHistory',
1354:       history,
1355:     });
1356:   }
1357: 
1358:   private async _ensureDefaultSession(initialLoad: boolean = false): Promise<void> {
1359:     const sessions = this._storageService.getSessions();
1360:     let activeId = this._getActiveSessionId();
1361: 
1362:     if (sessions.length === 0) {
1363:       const defaultSession: ChatSession = {
1364:         id: 'session_' + Date.now() + '_' + Math.random().toString(36).substring(2, 9),
1365:         title: 'New Session',
1366:         timestamp: Date.now(),
1367:         messages: [],
1368:         messageCount: 0,
1369:       };
1370:       sessions.push(defaultSession);
1371:       activeId = defaultSession.id;
1372:       await this._storageService.saveSessions(sessions);
1373:       await this._saveActiveSessionId(activeId);
1374:       // Send empty history for the new default session
1375:       if (initialLoad) {
1376:         this._sendChatHistoryToWebview();
1377:       }
1378:     } else if (!activeId || !sessions.find((s) => s.id === activeId)) {
1379:       activeId = sessions[0].id;
1380:       await this._saveActiveSessionId(activeId);
1381:       // Send history for the existing session we're switching to
1382:       if (initialLoad) {
1383:         this._sendChatHistoryToWebview();
1384:       }
1385:     }
1386:   }
1387: 
1388:   private async _createNewSession(): Promise<void> {
1389:     const sessions = this._storageService.getSessions();
1390:     const newSession: ChatSession = {
1391:       id: 'session_' + Date.now() + '_' + Math.random().toString(36).substring(2, 9),
1392:       title: 'New Session',
1393:       timestamp: Date.now(),
1394:       messages: [],
1395:       messageCount: 0,
1396:     };
1397:     sessions.unshift(newSession);
1398:     await this._storageService.saveSessions(sessions);
1399:     await this._saveActiveSessionId(newSession.id);
1400:     this._resetAgentPlanAndMemory();
1401: 
1402:     this._sendChatSessionsToWebview();
1403:     this._sendChatHistoryToWebview();
1404:   }
1405: 
1406:   private async _selectSession(sessionId: string): Promise<void> {
1407:     const sessions = this._storageService.getSessions();
1408:     const session = sessions.find((s) => s.id === sessionId);
1409:     if (session) {
1410:       await this._saveActiveSessionId(sessionId);
1411:       this._sendChatSessionsToWebview();
1412:       this._sendChatHistoryToWebview();
1413:     } else {
1414:       // Session not found in list — could be stale. Re-sync from storage.
1415:       this._sendChatSessionsToWebview();
1416:       vscode.window.showWarningMessage(`Session "${sessionId}" not found. Refreshing session list.`);
1417:     }
1418:   }
1419: 
1420:   private async _deleteSession(sessionId: string): Promise<void> {
1421:     const sessions = this._storageService.getSessions();
1422:     const activeId = this._getActiveSessionId();
1423: 
1424:     const filtered = sessions.filter((s) => s.id !== sessionId);
1425:     await this._storageService.saveSessions(filtered);
1426: 
1427:     // Also delete the messages key for this session
1428:     await this._storageService.deleteMessages(sessionId);
1429: 
1430:     if (activeId === sessionId) {
1431:       if (filtered.length > 0) {
1432:         await this._saveActiveSessionId(filtered[0].id);
1433:       } else {
1434:         await this._saveActiveSessionId('');
1435:         await this._ensureDefaultSession(true);
1436:       }
1437:     } else if (!activeId || !filtered.find((s) => s.id === activeId)) {
1438:       // Our active session was deleted but we're on a different session — ensure we have a valid one
1439:       await this._ensureDefaultSession(true);
1440:     }
1441: 
1442:     this._sendChatSessionsToWebview();
1443:     this._sendChatHistoryToWebview();
1444:   }
1445: 
1446:   private _getActiveSessionId(): string | undefined {
1447:     const id = this._context.workspaceState.get<string>('mirror-vs.activeSessionId');
1448:     if (id) return id;
1449:     // Fall back to file backup for cross-workspace compatibility
1450:     return this._storageService.getActiveSessionIdFromFile();
1451:   }
1452: 
1453:   private async _saveActiveSessionId(id: string): Promise<void> {
1454:     await this._context.workspaceState.update('mirror-vs.activeSessionId', id);
1455:     // Also persist to file backup
1456:     this._storageService.persistActiveSessionId(id);
1457:   }
1458: 
1459:   private _sendChatSessionsToWebview(): void {
1460:     if (!this._view) return;
1461:     const sessions = this._storageService.getSessions();
1462:     const activeSessionId = this._getActiveSessionId() || '';
1463:     // Use stored messageCount from metadata (faster than loading each session's messages)
1464:     const enrichedSessions: ChatSession[] = sessions.map((s) => ({
1465:       id: s.id,
1466:       title: s.title,
1467:       timestamp: s.timestamp,
1468:       messages: [],
1469:       messageCount: s.messageCount || 0,
1470:     }));
1471:     this._view.webview.postMessage({
1472:       type: 'updateChatSessions',
1473:       sessions: enrichedSessions,
1474:       activeSessionId,
1475:     });
1476:   }
1477: 
1478:   private _sendWorkspaceFileTokenSource: vscode.CancellationTokenSource | undefined;
1479: 
1480:   // Recursive glob patterns to find files at any directory depth.
1481:   // VS Code's findFiles automatically ignores standard system folders like node_modules via user settings.
1482:   private static readonly _WORKSPACE_GLOB_PATTERNS = [
1483:     '**/*.{ts,tsx,js,jsx,json,html,css,scss,py,rb,go,rs,md,yaml,yml,toml,sh,bash}',
1484:   ];
1485: 
1486:   private async _sendWorkspaceFiles() {
1487:     if (!this._view) return;
1488: 
1489:     // Cancel any previous pending scan
1490:     if (this._sendWorkspaceFileTokenSource) {
1491:       this._sendWorkspaceFileTokenSource.cancel();
1492:       this._sendWorkspaceFileTokenSource.dispose();
1493:     }
1494: 
1495:     try {
1496:       this._sendWorkspaceFileTokenSource = new vscode.CancellationTokenSource();
1497:       const token = this._sendWorkspaceFileTokenSource.token;
1498: 
1499:       // Run parallel recursive glob queries.
1500:       // Use AbortController-style cancellation via the token.
1501:       const allResults = await Promise.all(
1502:         MirrorVsSidebarProvider._WORKSPACE_GLOB_PATTERNS.map((pattern) =>
1503:           vscode.workspace.findFiles(pattern, undefined, 3000, token),
1504:         ),
1505:       );
1506: 
1507:       if (token.isCancellationRequested) return;
1508: 
1509:       // Deduplicate and flatten results
1510:       const seen = new Set<string>();
1511:       const files: string[] = [];
1512:       for (const results of allResults) {
1513:         for (const uri of results) {
1514:           const relPath = path.relative(vscode.workspace.workspaceFolders![0].uri.fsPath, uri.fsPath);
1515:           if (!seen.has(relPath)) {
1516:             seen.add(relPath);
1517:             files.push(relPath);
1518:           }
1519:         }
1520:       }
1521: 
1522:       // Cap at 3000 files to support extremely large codebases seamlessly
1523:       files.sort();
1524:       const cappedFiles = files.slice(0, 3000);
1525: 
1526:       this._view.webview.postMessage({
1527:         type: 'workspaceFiles',
1528:         files: cappedFiles,
1529:       });
1530:     } catch (e) {
1531:       console.warn('Workspace files fetch failed:', e);
1532:       // Fallback: send empty list gracefully
1533:       this._view?.webview.postMessage({ type: 'workspaceFiles', files: [] });
1534:     }
1535:   }
1536: 
1537:   public handleMirrorTask(task: string) {
1538:     // Receive a task from Mirror Assistant and send it to the webview
1539:     if (!this._view) return;
1540:     vscode.window.showInformationMessage(`🪞 New task from Mirror: ${task}`);
1541:     this._view.webview.postMessage({
1542:       type: 'mirrorTask',
1543:       task,
1544:     });
1545:   }
1546: 
1547:   public handleSelectionCommand(action: 'fix' | 'explain', text: string) {
1548:     if (!this._view) {
1549:       return;
1550:     }
1551:     if (!text.trim()) {
1552:       vscode.window.showWarningMessage('Please select some code in the active editor first!');
1553:       return;
1554:     }
1555: 
1556:     const formattedText =
1557:       action === 'fix'
1558:         ? `Fix the following code:\n\`\`\`\n${text}\n\`\`\``
1559:         : `Explain the following code:\n\`\`\`\n${text}\n\`\`\``;
1560: 
1561:     this._view.webview.postMessage({
1562:       type: 'prefillPrompt',
1563:       text: formattedText,
1564:     });
1565:   }

### 🎯 EXECUTION DISCIPLINE (HARD RULES)
1. **User Intent is Source of Truth**: The user's most recent message defines what success looks like. If they change direction, immediately abandon the outdated plan and discard obsolete goals.
2. **Completion Gate (MANDATORY)**: After EVERY read_file or grep_search call, ask yourself: "Can I write the patch right now with the information I have?" If YES → write the patch immediately. If NO → identify the ONE specific piece of missing information.
3. **Investigation Budget**: Max 6 read/search operations per task before you MUST either write a patch or explain what is missing. For trivial tasks, your budget is 2.
4. **Patch-First Workflow**: The correct sequence is always: Read → Patch → Verify. NOT: Read → Read → Read → Read → Patch.
5. **Never Re-Read Known Content**: Do NOT call read_file on the same file or line range you have already read in this session.
6. **Failure Recovery (Patch Failed)**: When a patch_file fails with "SEARCH block not found": read ONLY the exact section that contains the block you tried to match, copy the exact lines, and retry.

9. **On Failure, Simplify**: If a test fails or a patch doesn't apply, resist the urge to add more code or widen the scope. Step back, re-read the error, and try a simpler approach.
    10. **Strict Tool State Machine**: You are in either SEARCH MODE, PATCH MODE, or VERIFY MODE. You MUST output exactly ONE tool call per response. Outputting multiple tool calls or mixed-mode tool calls in a single response is strictly forbidden and will result in system rejection.

### 🐛 EVIDENCE-DRIVEN DEBUGGING DISCIPLINE (HARD RULES)
1. **No Guess-and-Patch Loops (Hypothesis Churn)**: Never propose patches based on blind speculation. A debugging process must be strictly evidence-driven: Observe Symptom → Identify Producer Component → Inspect Source Files → Form One Hypothesis → Prove Hypothesis → Patch → Re-test.
2. **Contradiction Invalidation**: If a patch fails to resolve the issue, immediately invalidate your previous hypothesis. Do NOT stack defensive layers (like adding locks, refs, or extra state checks) on top of a failed theory. Re-evaluate from first principles.
3. **Strict Source Ownership**: Never explain or guess the behavior of a listener, callback, event handler, service, hook, or component unless you have actually called `read_file` or `grep_search` and inspected its source code directly.
4. **Single Active Theory**: You are allowed exactly one active root-cause theory at a time. Discard on failure instead of layering.
5. **Evidence Before Complexity**: Do not add extra complexity unless you have collected concrete evidence that proves that specific event sequence is actually occurring.
6. **Require Ownership Discovery**: Before proposing or modifying code, you MUST discover and verify: (1) Which component owns this feature? (2) Which API owns this data? (3) Which service is the source of truth? Never write a patch until you know all three.
7. **Verify Data Models (No Inferred Schemas)**: Before filtering or accessing any field on an object or document (e.g. `doc.type === "invoice"`), you MUST call `read_file` or `grep_search` to inspect actual data usage and confirm the field exists and is populated exactly as assumed.

For JavaScript exceptions, you MUST retrieve the actual error message, stack trace, or diagnostic stack. Proposing patches based on generic exception names without traces is strictly prohibited.
9. **Architecture-First Feature Mapping**: For all feature requests, map the complete architectural flow (UI Component ➔ API Endpoint ➔ Database Schema ➔ Business Rules) before proposing or implementing changes.

142:     if (!chatScrollContainer || !chatMessages) return;

144:     if (userBubbles.length === 0) return;

30:

33:       return this._storageService.trimOldSessions(50);
34:     });
35:

69:   public async resolveWebviewView(

Based on my thorough review of all three frontend files (HTML, CSS, JS) and the sidebar provider, I now have enough context. Here is my analysis and recommended improvements:

---

## 🔍 Frontend Audit — Mirror VS Sidebar UI

I've reviewed all four core frontend files:
- `src/webview/sidebar.html` (635 lines) — Structure
- `src/webview/sidebar.css` (3799 lines) — Styling
- `src/webview/sidebar.js` (4636 lines) — Logic
- `src/providers/sidebar-provider.ts` (1567 lines) — Message bridge

---

### ✅ Strengths (What's Working Well)

| Area | Notes |
|------|-------|
| **Visual polish** | Excellent dark theme, glassmorphism effects, smooth CSS transitions, OLED-optimized palette. CSS custom properties are well-organized. |
| **Feature density** | Multi-provider switching, checkpoints, multi-diff review, artifacts, prompt templates, voice input — impressive breadth. |
| **Architecture** | Clean message-passing pattern (`vscode.postMessage` / `onDidReceiveMessage`) between webview and provider. |
| **Responsive drawers** | Smooth slide animations for settings, history, checkpoints, and multi-diff drawers. |
| **Accessibility basics** | Proper `role`, `aria-multiline`, `contenteditable` on the prompt input. |

---

### 🔴 Issues & Improvements Needed

#### 1. **CSS — External Font Import Blocks Rendering (Performance)**
**File:** `src/webview/sidebar.css` line 2
```css
@import url('https://fonts.googleapis.com/css2?family=Outfit:wght@300;400;500;600;700;800&family=JetBrains+Mono:wght@400;500;600&display=swap');
```
**Problem:** This `@import` blocks CSS parsing until the Google Fonts request completes (render-blocking). In a VS Code webview, this causes a visible flash of unstyled text (FOUT) and delays the entire UI from rendering.
**Fix:** Move font loading to a `<link rel="preload">` in the HTML `<head>` with `as="style"`, and use `font-display: swap` so text renders immediately with fallback fonts.

---

#### 2. **JS — 4636-Line Monolithic IIFE — No Modularization**
**File:** `src/webview/sidebar.js` — entire file is one giant `(function() { ... })();`
**Problem:** The entire frontend logic lives in a single file with no module boundaries. This makes:
- Debugging difficult (no clear separation of concerns)
- Collaboration harder (merge conflicts on one file)
- Testing impossible (no importable units)
**Fix:** Split into modules: `state.js`, `ui-renderer.js`, `message-handler.js`, `settings.js`, `checkpoints.js`, etc. Use ES modules or at minimum IIFE-namespaced sub-files.

---

#### 3. **JS — Missing Error Boundaries on vscode.postMessage**
**File:** `src/webview/sidebar.js` — dozens of `vscode.postMessage(...)` calls
**Problem:** If the VS Code API becomes unavailable (e.g., webview disposed mid-operation), these calls throw uncaught exceptions with no user-facing error feedback. Found in `sendMessage()`, `triggerSend()`, and all click handlers.
**Fix:** Wrap `vscode.postMessage` in a safe wrapper:
```js
function safePostMessage(msg) {
  try {
    vscode.postMessage(msg);
  } catch (e) {
    console.warn('[MirrorVS] postMessage failed:', e.message);
    showToast('Connection lost. Please reload the panel.', 'error');
  }
}
```

---

#### 4. **CSS+HTML — No Loading/Empty States for Chat Messages**
**File:** `src/webview/sidebar.html` line 466-510
**Problem:** The chat area only has a welcome card that disappears after the first message. There is no:
- **Loading skeleton** while waiting for AI responses (just a spinner appended to stream elements)
- **Empty state** when all messages are cleared from a session
- **Error state** when message loading fails
**Fix:** Add a dedicated `<div id="chat-loading-skeleton">` with a shimmer animation, and an `<div id="chat-empty-state">` for sessions with no messages.

---

#### 5. **JS — `updateStickyUserMessage` Called Too Frequently**
**File:** `src/webview/sidebar.js` function `updateStickyUserMessage()` (line 107)
**Problem:** This function queries all `.message.user` bubbles and resets their styles on **every** scroll event and **every** chat update. On a long conversation with dozens of messages, this causes jank.
**Fix:** Debounce the scroll handler to 16ms (one frame), and track the last user message reference so you only update when the DOM actually changes.

---

#### 6. **CSS — Massive File (3799 lines) Needs Organization**
**File:** `src/webview/sidebar.css`
**Problem:** All styles live in one file with no table of contents or section index. This makes it hard to find and modify specific component styles.
**Fix:** Add a clickable table of contents at the top with CSS anchor links, and split into logical sections with clear visual separators. Long-term: split into component CSS files.

---

#### 7. **HTML — No `<noscript>` Fallback or Error Boundary UI**
**File:** `src/webview/sidebar.html`
**Problem:** If JavaScript fails to load or execute (e.g., CSP blocks the script, or a syntax error crashes parsing), users see a completely blank dark panel with no indication of what went wrong.
**Fix:** Add a `<noscript>` tag and a hidden error boundary `<div>` that becomes visible if the IIFE init fails.

---

#### 8. **Accessibility — Missing Focus Indicators and Keyboard Navigation**
**Files:** All three
**Problem:**
- No visible `:focus-visible` outlines on interactive elements (buttons, selects, the contenteditable div)
- No `aria-label` on icon-only buttons (e.g., `#new-chat-btn`, `#toggle-history-btn`)
- The drawers cannot be closed with `Escape` key
- No `role="status"` or `aria-live` on the chat message area for screen readers to announce new messages
**Fix:** Add `:focus-visible` ring styles, `aria-label` attributes on all icon buttons, and an `Escape` key handler for drawers.

---

#### 9. **Security — `contenteditable` div has no XSS sanitization**
**File:** `src/webview/sidebar.html` line 547
```html
<div id="prompt-input" class="prompt-editable" contenteditable="true" ...></div>
```
**Problem:** Paste handlers and programmatic `innerHTML` setting could allow injection if the VS Code CSP ever weakens. The contenteditable div accepts arbitrary HTML on paste.
**Fix:** Strip all HTML tags on paste (only keep plain text), or use `textContent` consistently instead of `innerHTML` when programmatically setting the input.

---

#### 10. **JS — No State Management Pattern — Global Variables Everywhere**
**File:** `src/webview/sidebar.js` — variables like `activeFilePath`, `customApisList`, `promptTemplates`, `currentStreamElements` are scattered throughout the IIFE.
**Problem:** State mutations are unpredictable. Multiple functions read/write `activeFilePath` without a single source of truth.
**Fix:** Implement a simple state object with getter/setter proxies or a pub/sub pattern:
```js
const state = {
  _activeFilePath: '',
  get activeFilePath() { return this._activeFilePath; },
  set activeFilePath(val) { this._activeFilePath = val; renderContextBar(); }
};
```
